## DAMAGE-CLAIMS ##

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: How do I fix a failed payout? ---
Also asked as: Your Payout Failed / Action Required to Receive Your Pending Payout for Rentals

Direct the user to fix their bank account information immediately. The failed payout is caused by incorrect bank account numbers. Guide them through this process:

From the Owner app:
1. Go to your Neighbors Trailer account
2. Select "More" in the bottom-right corner  
3. Select "My Bank Account"
4. Enter the correct routing and account number

Common issues include account numbers that are too short or too long for the specified bank. The system will specify the exact issue (e.g., "account number is 9 digits long, while most account numbers at that bank are 10 long").

Important: Users will not receive funds sitting in their connected Stripe account until this is resolved. If they need assistance with the correction process, escalate to human support.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: Why am I getting non-compliance notices for not starting/ending rentals? ---
Also asked as: Non-Compliance Start / End Rental

Explain that owners are required to start and end rentals in the system at the actual pickup and return times. Non-compliance results in:
- Forfeiture of payout
- $25 daily fee for every day the booking remains open per Terms of Use

Why ending rentals promptly is critical:
1. You're holding back the renter's deposit money, which negatively impacts reviews and platform reputation
2. Your payout is only initiated when you end the rental
3. Delayed ending makes it difficult to prove damages were caused by the renter
4. Provides proof of actual rental completion date/time for late return fee disputes

Special circumstances: If the renter didn't show up, they need to cancel (not the owner) to avoid cancellation fees. If the trailer was abandoned or in an accident, advise them to contact support before ending the rental. For extensions, direct both parties to use the platform's extension request feature.

If the owner mentions working with Jeremy or other staff on a specific situation, acknowledge this and ask for the booking ID to review the guidance provided.

--- [Renter] [damage-claims] Q: Where do I pick up the trailer? ---
Also asked as: Re: Notification (when asking about pickup location)

Explain that pickup information is provided after booking acceptance:
- The trailer owner provides their address and phone number once they accept the booking
- Users can also message the trailer owner directly using "Send Message" on the listing page
- If they don't see the address after acceptance, check the Messages tab for owner communication
- The pickup location is the same as the return location

Do NOT provide specific addresses from staff emails. Direct them to check their Messages tab or contact the owner directly through the platform.

--- [Both] [damage-claims] Q: What should I do if I suspect a policy violation notice was sent in error? ---
Also asked as: Notice of Policy Violation / Action Required, Re: Notification (about deleted messages)

If a user claims they didn't violate platform policies, first review the situation. Our automated system is continuously learning and sometimes removes messages in error. 

For legitimate policy violations involving circumvention attempts:
- Users must contact the renter and guide them to create a booking on the platform within 48 hours
- Consequences apply regardless of whether the renter complies  
- Account suspension or minimum $200 deduction (or 30% of rent amount) from next payout
- Violations cannot be discussed by phone or support chat - only by email

For false positives (messages deleted in error):
- Acknowledge the automated system made an error
- Report to development team for resolution within 48 hours
- Apologize for inconvenience

Important: Any messages that are defamatory toward the platform to renters are considered violations.

--- [Both] [damage-claims] Q: How do I get receipts or invoices for bookings? ---
Also asked as: Re: Notification (asking for copies of invoices)

Direct users to access receipts through their booking details:

From the Website:
- Go to Booking Details
- Click the "Documents" tab  
- Download the receipt

From the App:
- Go to booking details
- Scroll down and select "Receipts"

For deposit deduction claims, the receipt will show the resolution details and any approved amounts. If they need clarification on a specific deduction decision, ask for the Booking ID to review the claim details.

--- [Renter] [damage-claims] Q: How do I leave a review? ---
Also asked as: Re: Notification (about leaving reviews), Re: insurance claim (when asking about reviews)

Provide step-by-step instructions for leaving reviews:

From the App:
- Select "Bookings"
- Select "Past"  
- Select "More"
- Select "Post a Review"

From the Web:
- From your Dashboard, select "My Booking"
- Select "Past Bookings"
- Select the 3 dots under Action
- Select "Post a Review"

Note that completed bookings automatically send a message with a clickable link requesting a review to both owner and renter.

--- [Both] [damage-claims] Q: What does it mean when my account is suspended or deactivated? ---
Also asked as: Your account has been deactivated, Account Suspension / Non-Compliance

Account suspension/deactivation occurs for several reasons:
- Non-compliance with policies (not adding bank information, not starting/ending rentals)
- Multiple policy violations
- Not completing required actions within 24 hours of notification
- Maintenance policy violations (e.g., trailer brakes not fixed)

Users are no longer authorized to use services until they contact support first. For bank information issues specifically, explain they cannot access their account to add the information while suspended - they must reply to the suspension email for assistance.

If they want clarification on the specific reason, direct them to respond to the deactivation email for additional information. Some suspensions allow appeals if applied in error.

--- [Both] [damage-claims] Q: How do I contact the trailer owner or get their information? ---
Also asked as: Re: Notification (asking how to contact owner), Re: trailer pick up

Explain the communication process:
- Message owners using "Send Message" on the listing page before booking
- After booking acceptance, owner's contact information is automatically shared
- If auto-share is disabled, owner will manually share contact details
- Check the Messages tab for owner communications

Important: Do NOT share direct contact information or addresses from staff emails. Always direct users to use the platform's messaging system first.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: How do I handle toll charges not associated with rentals? ---
Also asked as: Off-Platform Tolls

When owners receive toll notifications for charges not associated with platform rentals, explain:

You're being notified of tolls incurred while your trailer was enrolled in the toll program but not on an active rental. This notification serves two purposes:
1. You can use the attached toll report to recover fees from your renter if the trailer was rented during that time
2. The toll amount will be deducted from your next payout

If the license plate information is incorrect, advise them to provide the correct plate number for verification. Include the attached toll transaction report when available.

--- [Internal] [damage-claims] Q: How do I handle booking validation errors or technical issues? ---
Also asked as: Regarding Booking ID # (with validation problems)

For technical booking issues where the system shows validation errors:
1. Escalate to development team to resolve the validating error
2. Once resolved, notify the owner that the booking status has been changed to 'Accepted'
3. If the trailer is currently with the renter, they can now start the rental in the system
4. Always include the specific booking ID in communications

For platform outages, acknowledge the temporary technical issue and confirm when it has been resolved.

--- [Both] [damage-claims] Q: How do I file an insurance claim? ---
Also asked as: Re: insurance claim

Direct users to file insurance claims directly through the Neighbors Trailer claims form. Before beginning, they must gather:
1. Pictures of damages
2. Pictures of all 4 sides of the entire trailer
3. Picture of the VIN sticker  
4. Estimate for repairs

Provide this link to start the claim: https://form.jotform.com/Neighbors_Trailer/insurance-claim-form

For questions about the claims department specifically, direct them to contact: claims@neighborstrailer.com

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: How do I handle circumvention violations and payout deductions? ---
Also asked as: Payout Deduction Notice

When owners receive payout deductions for circumvention violations, explain that:

A circumvention occurs when you receive a booking or lead through Neighbors Trailer and offer rental services outside the platform. This includes sharing contact information before booking acceptance.

The deduction amount ($30-$200 or 30% of rent amount) has often been reduced from the full policy amount. Key points:
- Policy applies regardless of whether the rental actually happened
- Pictures and measurements should be shared through listings or platform messages
- This protects against high-risk situations (damage, theft, liability)
- Maintains platform insurance and protection coverage
- Ensures fair treatment for all trailer owners

If they're concerned about the deduction, acknowledge their frustration but explain this protects the platform's investment in bringing qualified rentals.

--- [Both] [damage-claims] Q: How do I check my trailer listing approval status? ---
Also asked as: Re: Notification (asking about listing approval), Re: Update Listing

Listings are typically approved within 4-6 hours, but may take 1-2 business days depending on queue volume. To check status:

App: More > My Trailers (look for green/red status indicator)
Web: Dashboard > Trailer > Trailer List

Common approval delays:
- Contact information in trailer photos  
- Incomplete address in Location field
- Incorrect 17-character VIN
- Weight capacity showing total trailer weight instead of load capacity only
- Incomplete profile or ID verification

If they made changes and resubmitted, future approvals will be much quicker. For urgent situations requiring immediate approval, escalate to human support.

--- [Renter] [damage-claims] Q: How do I add or update my insurance for a booking? ---
Also asked as: Re: Verification Code (when asking about insurance)

If a renter is having trouble adding insurance to their booking, ask for the Booking ID to investigate the specific issue. 

For verification codes related to insurance setup, explain that the code goes on the verification screen in their Neighbors Trailer account - they would have been on this screen to receive the code.

If insurance didn't go through during booking, they may need to contact support with the specific booking details to add it retroactively.

--- [Both] [damage-claims] Q: How do QR codes and trailer shop items work? ---
Also asked as: Re: Notification (asking about QR codes)

For QR code stickers and decals, direct users to the Neighbors Trailer Shop at: https://resources.neighborstrailer.com/shop/

The QR codes help potential renters quickly access trailer listings. Users don't get individual QR codes for each trailer - the shop provides general promotional materials.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: What should I know about Stripe account issues? ---
Also asked as: Re: Notification (about Stripe blocks)

If owners receive notifications about Stripe account blocks/restrictions, first check if the issue has been automatically resolved. Often no manual action is needed.

If the Stripe account is currently enabled and working, reassure them no further action is required. If there are ongoing issues, escalate to human support to investigate the specific Stripe connection problem.

--- [Both] [damage-claims] Q: How do extension requests work? ---
Also asked as: Re: Notification (about extensions), Re: Contact us query (extension problems)

Extension requests can be submitted by either the renter or trailer owner:

From Website:
- Go to Dashboard > Bookings > Current/Upcoming Bookings
- Select the applicable booking  
- Click Extension Request
- Enter additional days and remarks
- Click Send Request

From App:
- Select Bookings > Current/Upcoming
- Open the booking
- Select Extension Request  
- Enter additional days and remarks
- Tap Send Request

The other party will be notified and can accept the extension. Payment for additional days is processed upon acceptance.

If extension requests aren't working, ask for the specific booking number to investigate technical issues.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: How do I file a damage claim after a rental? ---
Also asked as: How can I file a damage claim?

Direct the user to file a Deposit Deduction Claim when ending the rental. Provide these exact steps:

From the App:
1. Select "Bookings"
2. Open the applicable booking under "Current" 
3. Tap "End Rental"
4. Select the "Deposit Deduction Claim" option
5. Enter required details describing the damage or loss
6. Upload supporting photos
7. Tap "End Rental" to submit the claim

From the Website:
1. Go to Dashboard
2. Select "Bookings" 
3. Open the applicable booking under "Current Bookings"
4. Click "End Rental"
5. Check the "Deposit Deduction Claim" box
6. Enter required information
7. Upload supporting photos
8. Select "End Rental" to submit the claim

For damages over $500 with NT Protect: If damages exceed $500 and the rental included NT Protect Protection Package, the owner can also file a protection claim by selecting "File Claim" button on the booking details page for any On Rent or Completed booking.

Tell owners to gather before filing:
- Before-and-after photos
- Detailed description of damage
- Repair estimates or invoices (if available)

Explain that the renter will be notified and may dispute within 24 hours. Neighbors Trailer will then review all information and make a determination.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: Can I still file a damage claim after I've already ended the rental without claiming damages? ---
Also asked as: I found some damage on my trailer and did not initially claim any deductible. The rental has not been paid out yet. Can I still put in a claim?

If the rental has not been paid out yet, tell the owner they can still file a claim. Direct them to provide:
1. Booking ID number
2. What was damaged
3. How much they wish to deduct (if possible)  
4. Images showing the damage

However, if they already ended the rental without selecting the Deposit Deduction Claim option, they cannot go back and add a claim through the normal process. The system only allows damage claims to be submitted during the "End Rental" process.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: How do I cancel or remove a damage claim I already submitted? ---
Also asked as: I would like to remove the deposit deduction claim

Tell the owner to contact support directly requesting cancellation of their Deposit Deduction Claim. Provide the specific booking ID when contacting support.

Explain that once a claim is cancelled, the renter's deposit will be released accordingly.

Note: This requires manual intervention by support staff and cannot be done by the owner through the platform directly.

--- [Renter] [damage-claims] Q: How do I dispute a damage claim made against me? ---
Also asked as: These claims are untrue. The ramp support bars were not bent and the dent in the box was not there.

Explain that renters have 24 hours to dispute damage claims. If they receive notification of a damage claim:

1. They can dispute by responding within 24 hours
2. They should provide evidence that the damage existed before their rental (such as listing photos showing pre-existing damage)
3. They can upload photos from the listing that show damage already present
4. After 24 hours, the window to dispute closes and the claim may be approved

Tell renters to check their account/booking details to view the full claim information and evidence provided by the owner.

--- [Both] [damage-claims] Q: What information do I need to check the status of a damage claim? ---
Also asked as: Could you please advise as to what the individual claimed for damages and what if any amounts were given to him?

Direct users to log into their account on the Neighbors Trailer app or website and navigate to the specific booking number. All claim details including:
- Description of claimed damages
- Photos submitted
- Deduction amounts assessed
- Current status

Will be visible in the booking details page.

If the 24-hour dispute window has passed, inform them that the claim has been processed and they can view the final determination in their booking details.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: How do I submit a major damage claim or total loss claim? ---
Also asked as: The trailer has sustained structural failure and is considered a total loss

For major damage or total loss situations:

1. First submit a Deposit Deduction Claim when ending the rental (up to the full deposit amount)
2. File an NT Protect claim by selecting "File Claim" from the booking details page
3. Gather comprehensive documentation:
   - Photos of all damage from multiple angles
   - Pictures of all 4 sides of the trailer
   - Photo of the VIN sticker  
   - Detailed repair estimates or total loss valuation
   - Any police reports or incident documentation

Explain that NT Protect provides up to $25,000 coverage with a $500 deductible for eligible damage during verified rental periods.

Tell owners that once a claim is submitted, it goes to the NT Support team and they will be contacted via email if updates or additional information is needed.

--- [Both] [damage-claims] Q: How long does it take to process damage claims? ---
Also asked as: I submitted a damage claim and am looking to check on the status. I have not had any updates since I submitted the claim.

Inform users that the NT Protect Team processes each claim as soon as possible, but processing times vary depending on claim complexity and documentation required.

For claim status updates, direct them to contact the claims team directly at Claims@NTProtect.net.

Explain that they will be emailed as soon as there are updates, and to check their booking details page for current status information.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: What should I do if a renter reports damage during the rental? ---
Also asked as: On my way to renter after him calling and saying, Axel may be broke. Please respond back as soon as possible.

Provide immediate guidance:

1. **Safety First**: If the damage makes the trailer unsafe to tow, stop using immediately and arrange safe pickup/return
2. **Document Everything**: Take clear photos of damage and related issues - these are crucial for claims
3. **End Rental with Claim**: When getting the trailer back:
   - Go to Current Bookings
   - Select "End Rental" 
   - Check "Deposit Deduction Claim" box
   - Upload photos of damage
   - Include detailed description
   - Submit the claim
4. **NT Protect Claim**: If repair costs exceed $500 and booking included Protection Package, also file NT Protect claim by selecting "File Claim" from booking details
5. **Get Repair Estimates**: Collect estimates or invoices to support the claim

Ask for the booking number to provide specific assistance with their situation.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: The renter was not available for pickup and missed their rental - what do I do? ---
Also asked as: Customer was provided with my phone number at time of booking, and I was never contacted by them through a call/text or through the app

When a renter no-shows or fails to pick up:

1. Document the no-show situation with photos showing you were at the agreed location and time
2. Try to contact the renter through the platform messaging system
3. Contact Neighbors Trailer support immediately with the booking ID
4. Provide any evidence that you were available at the scheduled time and location (screenshots of messages, location photos, etc.)

Support will investigate and may cancel the booking, potentially allowing you to collect a cancellation fee if the renter was at fault.

Do not end the rental yourself if the trailer was never picked up - contact support for proper handling.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: Can I charge for additional days if the renter keeps my trailer longer due to damage/accident? ---
Also asked as: The original rental period was April 3-6, 2026. The renter abandoned the trailer following an accident, leading to a Florida Highway Patrol-ordered tow. I only regained possession on April 13.

For situations where the renter's actions (accidents, abandonment) prevent normal return:

Explain that renters are liable for rental fees until the trailer is properly returned. Document everything:
- Original rental dates
- Incident details (accident reports, police involvement)
- Date you regained possession
- Any tow/recovery costs incurred

Contact support with:
- Booking ID
- Detailed timeline of events
- Supporting documentation (police reports, tow receipts)
- Request for additional rental charges at standard daily rate

This requires manual review by the billing team as it's outside normal extension processes. The team will evaluate circumstances and determine appropriate additional charges.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: How do I handle situations where my trailer needs inspection after an accident? ---
Also asked as: The trailer is ready for inspection whenever you're ready

For accident damage requiring inspection:

1. Secure the trailer at your property and document the location
2. Take comprehensive photos of all damage from multiple angles  
3. Document the trailer's condition and any safety concerns
4. Coordinate with support team for inspection scheduling
5. Keep the trailer accessible but secure until inspection is complete

Provide the exact address where the trailer can be inspected. Support and claims teams will coordinate scheduling with you directly.

Do not attempt to move or repair the trailer until inspection and documentation is complete.

--- [Both] [damage-claims] Q: What should I know about insurance coverage for damage claims? ---
URL: https://neighborstrailer.com/help-center-details/Are-trailers-covered-by-insurance--58

Explain that trailer damage is covered by NT Protect during verified rental periods. Coverage provides up to $25,000 with a $500 deductible.

Important details:
- Coverage only applies during active "On Rent" period when platform procedures are followed correctly
- Protection Package is paid by renter at booking, not by owners
- If deductible cannot be collected from renter, the trailer owner is responsible for the $500 deductible
- For insurance questions, direct users to review the Terms of Use at https://neighborstrailer.com/terms

For specific insurance inquiries from third parties (like USAA claims), direct them to contact American Modern at +1 (800-695-1007) or JCook@amig.com with their claim reference number.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: How do I request Certificate of Insurance (COI) for a renter? ---
Also asked as: COI for booking ID 24857 and 24850

When renters request COI documentation, owners should contact support directly with:
- The booking ID(s) 
- Renter's name
- Specific request for COI

Support will provide the Certificate of Insurance directly to the requesting party, typically as an email attachment referencing the specific booking numbers.

--- [Policy] [damage-claims] Q: What happens when accounts are sent to collections for unpaid damages? ---
Also asked as: Yes, I don't think the renter has any plans to pay. Would you like us to send the 18 days of unpaid rental fees to collections?

When owners indicate a renter will not pay for damages or unpaid fees:

Support will ask owners directly: "Regarding booking ID [number], would you like us to send the [amount/duration] of unpaid rental fees to collections?"

If owner confirms, support provides collection agency with:
- Renter's full contact information (email, phone, address)
- Amount owed
- Trailer owner contact information (CC'd on communication)  
- Supporting documentation/attachments

The collection agency (Debt Collectors International) handles recovery attempts on behalf of the trailer owner.

--- [Internal] [damage-claims] Q: How do I handle circumvention violations related to damage situations? ---
Also asked as: I think it would be a good idea for yall to delete my account. I'm not sure who you think is in charge but this is my equipment and I don't need this app if that's how yall are gonna act

When owners attempt to circumvent the platform or violate terms during damage situations:

Send the standard policy violation notice explaining:
- Specific violation (circumvention attempt)
- Required action (must contact renter to create proper booking)
- Consequences (account suspension or minimum $200 deduction from next payout)
- Reference to Terms of Use abuse policy

Important: The violation consequence applies regardless of whether the renter complies. Even if the renter won't book through the platform, the policy violation still stands.

All circumvention discussions must be handled via email only - not by phone or chat.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: How do I file a damage claim for my trailer? ---
Direct the owner to use the "File Claim" button on the booking details page from any On Rent or Completed booking. Before they begin, they must gather:
1. Pictures of damages
2. Pictures of all 4 sides of their entire trailer
3. Picture of the VIN sticker
4. Estimate for repairs

If they experience an error submitting the claim in the app, suggest these troubleshooting steps:
1. Try signing out and signing back in
2. Ensure the app is up to date
3. Try using the website instead of the app or vice versa

For damage claims over $200, or if the app won't accept their claim amount, instruct them to email all supporting documentation (itemized invoices, repair quotes, and photos) directly to service@neighborstrailer.com. Tell them the team will need time to thoroughly review everything.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: What happens after I submit a damage claim? ---
Explain that once they submit a claim, it goes to the NT Protect team for review. There is no guaranteed timeline, but claims are typically reviewed within 30 days. The NT Protect team will contact them directly via email once there's an update.

If the claim was submitted more than 30 days ago and they haven't heard back, tell them to email again for a status update, but clarify that the NT Protect team works through claims as fast as possible and will reach out when there's news.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: How do I charge a renter for damage under $500? ---
If the damage is under $500 and they need to charge the renter directly (not through insurance), instruct them to:
1. Provide photos of the damage
2. Provide the receipt/estimate for replacement/repair
3. Provide the booking ID
4. Notify the renter through the platform about the damage and repair costs

Tell them that Neighbors Trailer can then attempt to charge the renter on their behalf. This process is separate from the NT Protect insurance claims.

--- [Renter] [damage-claims] Q: How do I dispute a deposit deduction claim? ---
When an owner files a deposit deduction claim, the renter will be contacted via email about the dispute process. They have 24 hours to respond with their dispute. The staff will then review both sides and make a determination.

If a renter claims damage was due to mechanical failure or pre-existing conditions, they should provide detailed explanations and any supporting evidence (photos, mechanic assessments, etc.).

--- [Both] [damage-claims] Q: Who is responsible for tire damage during a rental? ---
Explain tire damage responsibility based on cause:

Renter is responsible if damage occurred during rental due to:
- Hitting a curb or road hazard
- Nail or puncture
- Overloading the trailer
- Driving at speeds beyond tire's rated limit
- Any impact-related damage

Owner is responsible if damage was due to:
- Tire is 3 years old or older
- Tire defects
- Low tread
- Improper maintenance
- Improper installation

To determine tire age, check the 4-digit DOT date code on the sidewall. First two digits = week manufactured, last two digits = year. Example: 2522 means 25th week of 2022.

If there's a dispute about tire age, the owner must provide within 24 hours:
- Picture of tire sidewall showing date stamp
- Tire purchase receipt
- Estimated purchase date

--- [Both] [damage-claims] Q: What does NT Protect insurance cover? ---
NT Protect covers trailer damage during verified rental periods up to $25,000 with a $500 deductible. Coverage is paid for by the renter at booking - owners are not charged.

IMPORTANT: NT Protect only covers the trailer itself. If a renter causes a crash or damages someone else's vehicle, the renter's auto insurance policy would be liable, not NT Protect.

The $500 deductible applies to all eligible claims. If the deductible cannot be collected from the renter, the trailer owner is responsible for the $500 deductible amount.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: Can I get a partial deposit refund after filing a claim? ---
Once an owner has claimed the full deposit and submitted damage claims, they cannot issue partial refunds directly. If damages are less than expected or some charges (like tolls) are resolved separately, the deposit deduction stands as filed.

If the repair quote exceeds the $500 insurance deductible, the deposit will be applied toward the deductible balance and no refund will be issued to the renter.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: How do I handle late return fees and unpaid rental days? ---
When ending a rental with unpaid rental fees, use the "Deposit Deduction Claim" option and enter the required information. For late returns, calculate the prorated amount based on your daily rate.

If a renter extends their rental and still returns late, or books for fewer days but keeps the trailer longer, you can claim additional rental days at a prorated rate. Provide the booking details and explain the overage situation.

--- [Renter] [damage-claims] Q: What if I can't get my deposit refund due to a closed bank account? ---
If the original payment method is closed, Neighbors Trailer cannot redirect deposit funds to an alternate payment method or third party. 

If the trailer owner has submitted a deposit deduction claim and the renter wants the owner to retain the deposit and pay them directly outside the platform, the renter must confirm this arrangement in writing. Note that Neighbors Trailer will not be responsible for ensuring or enforcing payment from the trailer owner - any such arrangement is strictly between the renter and owner.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: How do I handle toll charges from a rental? ---
If you receive a toll bill for charges incurred during a rental, reply to service@neighborstrailer.com with the toll bill and Neighbors Trailer will attempt to charge the renter.

Before sending the toll bill, enroll in the free toll program to prevent future manual toll handling:
1. Login to your account and go to dashboard
2. Select "Enroll in Our Free Toll Program" 
3. Select "Click Here" (web) or "Tap Here" (app)
4. Select "Enroll Now"
5. Select "Add License Plate"
6. Select "Enroll"

The toll program is completely free with no subscription cost and automates toll collection from renters.

--- [Both] [damage-claims] Q: What should I do if there's an accident during the rental? ---
For accidents involving the trailer:
1. File a claim using the "File Claim" button on the booking details page
2. Gather all required documentation:
   - Pictures of damages
   - Pictures of all 4 sides of the trailer
   - Picture of VIN sticker
   - Repair estimates
3. Submit to NT Protect for review

The claim goes to NT Protect regardless of fault. If the trailer was rear-ended or hit by another vehicle, the same NT Protect claim process applies.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: The renter didn't show up but I started checkout - what should I do? ---
If you wait past the agreed pickup time and the renter doesn't communicate or show up, you can mark it as "No-Show" when ending the rental. Document the timeline of events including:
- Agreed pickup time
- When you messaged the renter for ETA
- How long you waited
- When you completed the checkout process

Provide this information if contacted by support for clarification about the booking.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: I can't end my rental due to app issues - what do I do? ---
If the app shows a white screen or error when trying to end a rental, contact support with:
1. Screenshot of the error (if any)
2. Date and time the trailer was returned
3. Condition the trailer was returned in
4. 4 photos of the trailer
5. Written permission for support to manually end the rental on your behalf

Support can then complete the process manually. This ensures accurate documentation and deactivates toll tracking for enrolled trailers.

--- [Renter] [damage-claims] Q: What should I do if a trailer owner asks for my driver's license to verify I'm not a scammer? ---
Direct the renter to contact support if an owner requests personal identification documents outside of the platform. Per Neighbors Trailer policy, owners who request driver's licenses or other personal documents from renters can have their accounts deactivated for non-compliance. The platform handles all verification processes internally. If a renter encounters this situation, escalate to human support for account review and potential owner discipline.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: I found damage after ending a rental - can I still file a claim for damage I discovered later? ---
Inform the owner that deposit deduction claims (DDCs) must be submitted BEFORE ending the rental. If a rental has already been ended without filing a DDC, and the renter's deposit has been returned, the owner cannot retroactively claim the deposit through the platform. In this case, direct the owner to file a claim with their own insurance policy for the damages. Emphasize the importance of completing thorough inspections and submitting DDCs before clicking "End Rental" to avoid this situation in the future.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: How do I file a deposit deduction claim for trailer damage? ---
Instruct the owner to submit a Deposit Deduction Claim (DDC) when ending the rental. The process is:

1. When ending the rental, select the "Deposit Deduction Claim" box at the bottom
2. Upload images clearly showing the damage that occurred during the rental
3. If damages exceed the deposit amount, include estimated repair costs in the claim notes
4. Complete the end rental process

After submitting the DDC, the renter has 24 hours to respond or dispute the claim before it is automatically approved and the deposit is transferred to the owner's account.

IMPORTANT: The DDC must be filed BEFORE ending the rental. Once a rental is ended without filing a DDC, the deposit cannot be claimed retroactively.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: How do I file an NT Protect claim for major damage over $500? ---
Direct the owner to file an NT Protect claim using this process:

1. First, file a Deposit Deduction Claim (DDC) when ending the rental to secure the $500 deductible
2. Gather required documentation:
   - Pictures of all damages
   - Pictures of all 4 sides of the entire trailer
   - Picture of the VIN sticker
   - Written repair estimate from a shop

3. Complete the NT Protect claim form at: https://form.jotform.com/Neighbors_Trailer/nt-protect-claim-form

NT Protect covers up to $25,000 in damages with a $500 deductible. The booking must have included the Protection Package for coverage to apply. Many owners use the deposit to cover the $500 deductible.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: What if the renter was in an accident but wasn't at fault - should I still file a deposit deduction claim? ---
Explain that filing a DDC is at the owner's discretion. If the owner intends to go through the renter's personal auto insurance for the damage, do not advise filing a DDC. However, if the booking was covered by NT Protect and the owner chooses to file a claim through NT Protect, many owners use the deposit to cover the $500 deductible. The owner should decide based on which route they prefer to pursue for damage recovery.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: A renter admitted fault and agreed to pay additional charges beyond the deposit - how do I process this? ---
If a renter admits fault and agrees to additional charges beyond the deposit amount, contact support with:
- The booking ID number
- Details of the damage amount
- Documentation showing the renter's agreement (text messages, emails, etc.)

Support can process additional charges to the renter's card on file beyond the deposit amount. This typically requires clear documentation of the renter's consent to the additional charges.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: What should I do if I accidentally ended a rental without filing a damage claim? ---
If an owner accidentally ended a rental without submitting a DDC and there was damage, provide these steps:
1. Contact support immediately with photos of the damage
2. Support will review the situation and may be able to process a claim internally
3. If the system has already processed the rental as complete and returned the deposit, the owner may need to pursue the claim through their own insurance

IMPORTANT: Emphasize that owners should always complete their inspection and file any necessary DDCs BEFORE clicking "End Rental" to avoid this situation.

--- [Renter] [damage-claims] Q: An owner filed a deposit deduction claim - how do I dispute it? ---
Explain that renters have 24 hours from when a DDC is submitted to respond or dispute the claim. During this period, the renter can:
1. Review the claim details in their booking
2. Dispute the claim if they believe it's unwarranted
3. Provide evidence supporting their dispute

The claims team will use reasonable judgment to determine liability and whether the dispute will be successful. If the renter doesn't respond within 24 hours, the claim is automatically approved and the deposit is transferred to the owner.

--- [Renter] [damage-claims] Q: Will the deposit count toward the $500 NT Protect deductible if there's major damage? ---
Confirm that yes, when a booking is covered by NT Protect and damages exceed $500, the owner can claim the renter's deposit to cover the $500 deductible. This is a common practice - the deposit serves as the deductible payment, and NT Protect covers eligible damages above $500 up to the policy limit of $25,000.

--- [Internal] [damage-claims] Q: How do I handle requests for rental agreements from insurance companies or legal entities? ---
When insurance companies, legal entities, or ticket authorities request rental agreements, provide the documentation immediately. Include all relevant details such as:
- License plate number
- Trailer VIN
- Complete rental agreement
- Photos if requested
- Any supporting documentation

If initial documents are rejected for missing information (like license plate or VIN), provide amended versions with the required details included.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: What if a renter damaged my trailer and then never returned it? ---
For situations involving unreturned trailers with damage:
1. Verify the renter took possession of the trailer
2. If confirmed, escalate to management immediately
3. Document all communications and evidence
4. The situation may require legal action
5. If the renter's account shows policy violations, consider account suspension

Advise the owner that NT Protect may apply if the booking included coverage, but theft/non-return situations require special handling beyond standard damage claims.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: Can I get reimbursed for damaged accessories like trailer jacks, chains, or other equipment? ---
Inform the owner that accessory damage follows the same process as trailer damage:
1. File a DDC when ending the rental for items under the deposit amount
2. For expensive accessories, include them in an NT Protect claim if total damages exceed $500 and the booking included coverage
3. Document the damage with photos and repair estimates
4. Small accessory damage (under deposit amount) is typically handled through the DDC process

--- [Both] [damage-claims] Q: What constitutes normal wear and tear versus renter responsibility? ---
Refer to the tire damage guidelines as a model, but explain that responsibility depends on the cause:

Renter is responsible for damage caused by use during the rental:
- Impact damage (hitting curbs, obstacles)
- Overloading the trailer beyond capacity
- Misuse or negligent operation
- Any damage that occurs due to how the trailer was operated

Owner is responsible for:
- Normal wear and tear from age
- Pre-existing conditions
- Equipment failures due to lack of maintenance
- Items that should have been replaced due to age (like tires over 3 years old)

Each situation requires individual review. When there's a dispute, Neighbors Trailer reviews circumstances and supporting documentation to make a determination.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: What photos do I need when filing damage claims? ---
For deposit deduction claims, require:
- Minimum of 4 photos of the trailer taken at return
- Clear photos showing specific damage
- Photos should clearly document the damage that occurred during the rental

For NT Protect claims, require:
- Pictures of all damages
- Pictures of all 4 sides of the entire trailer  
- Picture of the VIN sticker
- Written repair estimate from a qualified shop

Emphasize that clear documentation is essential for successful claims processing.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: How long do I have to file a damage claim? ---
Deposit deduction claims must be filed when ending the rental - there is no grace period. Once the rental is ended without filing a DDC, the opportunity to claim the deposit is lost. For NT Protect claims, direct owners to file as soon as possible after discovering damage and obtaining repair estimates. Do not specify exact timeframes for NT Protect claims without confirming current policy terms.

--- [Both] [damage-claims] Q: What if I disagree with a damage claim decision? ---
If either party disagrees with a damage claim decision, they can:
1. Provide additional evidence to support their position
2. Request a review by escalating to human support
3. Per Terms of Use, Neighbors Trailer reviews circumstances and supporting documentation before making final determinations
4. The company's decision process considers all available evidence and follows established policies

Note that damage claim disputes require thorough documentation and may involve management review for final resolution.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: How do I submit a damage claim for my trailer? ---
When a trailer owner reports damage from a rental, guide them through the proper claims process based on the damage amount and whether insurance was purchased.

For damages covered by the deposit amount:
- Direct them to submit a Deposit Deduction Claim (DDC) when ending the rental
- Instruct them to select the "Deposit Deduction Claim" box at the bottom when ending the rental
- They must upload images displaying the damages that occurred
- If damages exceed the deposit amount, tell them to include the estimated damage cost in the claim notes
- Once submitted, the renter has 24 hours to respond before the claim is approved and money is deposited

For damages exceeding $500 with insurance coverage:
- Direct them to file an insurance claim using the Neighbors Trailer claims form: https://form.jotform.com/Neighbors_Trailer/insurance-claim-form
- Before starting the claim, they need to gather:
  1. Pictures of damages
  2. Pictures of all 4 sides of their entire trailer
  3. Picture of the VIN sticker
  4. Estimate for repairs

IMPORTANT: They cannot file an insurance claim until the trailer has been returned. If they contact you before the rental ends, tell them to wait until the trailer is back in their possession.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: How do I end a rental and document damage? ---
Direct the owner to end the rental immediately upon trailer return and document any damage properly.

From the Neighbors Trailer App:
- Open the app and sign in
- Select Bookings → Current → Select applicable booking → End Rental
- Upload minimum of four new photos taken at time of return
- Confirm return date and time
- Enter relevant remarks
- If no damage: Tap End Rental to complete
- If damage exists: Select Deposit Deduction Claim option, enter required information, then tap End Rental

From the Website:
- Sign in at NeighborsTrailer.com → Dashboard → Bookings → Current Bookings
- Select End Rental for applicable booking
- Upload minimum of four new photos taken at time of return
- Confirm return date and time
- Enter relevant remarks
- If no damage: Select End Rental to complete
- If damage exists: Check Deposit Deduction Claim box, enter required information, then select End Rental

IMPORTANT: Ending the rental promptly ensures accurate documentation and deactivates toll tracking for enrolled trailers. Once a rental is ended, it cannot be reverted to a previous status.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: When am I responsible for tire damage versus the renter? ---
Explain tire damage responsibility based on cause and tire condition.

Renter is responsible when damage was caused during rental by:
- Hitting a curb or road hazard
- Nail or puncture
- Overloading the trailer
- Driving at speeds beyond tire's rated limit
- Any impact-related damage

Owner is responsible when damage is due to:
- Normal wear and tear, age, or improper maintenance
- Tire is 3 years old or older (tires should not exceed 3 years)
- Tire defects
- Low tread
- Improper installation

To determine tire age, direct them to locate the 4-digit DOT date code on tire sidewall:
- First two digits = week of manufacture
- Last two digits = year of manufacture
- Example: 2522 = 25th week of 2022

Note: This is a general guideline. Terms of Use may contain additional language. If there's a dispute, Neighbors Trailer will review circumstances and documentation before making a determination.

--- [Both] [damage-claims] Q: What is the NT Protect insurance deductible? ---
The NT Protect insurance has a $500 deductible that applies to all eligible damage claims.

If the deductible cannot be collected from the renter, the trailer owner becomes responsible for the $500 deductible amount.

The Protection Package fee is paid by the renter at booking time - trailer owners are not charged for the Protection Package itself.

--- [Renter] [damage-claims] Q: How does damage coverage work for rentals? ---
Explain coverage based on whether the booking includes insurance.

For bookings WITH insurance (NT Protect):
- Trailer damage is covered up to $25,000 during verified rental periods
- $500 deductible applies
- If damages meet or exceed $500 and renter is at fault, the trailer owner can file an insurance claim
- Renter is responsible for the $500 deductible

For bookings WITHOUT insurance:
- Neighbors Trailer reviews damage claims using fair judgment to determine liability
- If renter is determined at fault, they pay for all damages incurred
- If damages equal or less than deposit: owner can claim from deposit
- If damages exceed deposit: renter must pay the remaining amount

IMPORTANT: The renter is responsible for the trailer and any accessories while in their possession, regardless of insurance status.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: My renter says their insurance will cover the damage - what should I do? ---
If a renter wants to file through their own insurance because they're at fault:
- End the rental immediately and retain as much of their deposit as necessary to cover the deductible
- Their insurance deductible may differ from NT Protect's $500 deductible
- This is often the best option if the renter is clearly at fault

However, most insurance policies have deductibles. Only consider accepting their insurance coverage if they provide a letter of coverage from their insurance company that includes:
- Coverage for 100% of damages
- Coverage for replacement of license plate (if applicable)
- No deductible or gaps in coverage

Otherwise, process the claim through normal channels and let the renter seek reimbursement from their insurance later.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: The damage exceeds my deposit amount - what are my options? ---
When damages exceed the deposit, owners have multiple options based on insurance coverage.

If the booking included insurance and damages exceed $500:
- File an insurance claim using: https://form.jotform.com/Neighbors_Trailer/insurance-claim-form
- Gather required documentation before starting claim
- The renter will be responsible for the $500 deductible

If no insurance or damages under $500:
- Submit a Deposit Deduction Claim for the full deposit amount
- Include estimated damage costs in the claim notes
- After the DDC is approved, Neighbors Trailer may charge the renter for additional amounts
- The renter will be subject to pay the full damage amount beyond the deposit

When submitting the DDC, clearly document all damage with photos and provide repair estimates in the notes section.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: How long does it take to receive claim payouts? ---
For approved Deposit Deduction Claims:
- Payout is automatically initiated along with the rent payout
- Funds typically arrive in 1-3 business days in your bank account
- The claim amount is paid in addition to your rental earnings

For insurance claims:
- Processing times vary as they go through the third-party insurance provider
- Contact the insurance provider directly for status updates on active claims

The "Payout" status in your dashboard only refers to rental earnings and may not include approved claims until they're processed together.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: Can I return a deposit to my renter after filing a claim? ---
If you want to return a deposit after a Deposit Deduction Claim has been completed:

The claimed amount has already been paid out to your account along with your rental earnings. To process a return:
- Neighbors Trailer must withdraw your entire payout
- Refund the claimed amount to the renter  
- Re-initiate your payout
- A 5% admin fee applies for these transaction processes

Alternative: You can return the money to your renter directly, which Neighbors Trailer will not prohibit in this situation. This is often easier than going through the reversal process.

--- [Both] [damage-claims] Q: What should I do if I receive reports of reckless driving during a rental? ---
If you receive reports of dangerous driving during an active rental, this is treated as an emergency situation.

Contact Neighbors Trailer support immediately and provide:
- Your booking ID
- Details of the reports you've received
- Request the renter's contact information to address the situation directly

Support can provide the renter's phone number so you can contact them immediately to address safety concerns before potential damage or injury occurs.

The insurance covers damages above the deductible amount, up to $25,000 in coverage.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: My trailer was involved in an accident but there's no damage to my trailer - do I need to file a claim? ---
If there is no damage to your trailer, you cannot file a damage claim. Claims are only for actual physical damage to the trailer.

If your insurance company has contacted you about an incident, but your trailer has no damage, simply inform them there are no damages to claim.

If you believe there is additional information Neighbors Trailer should know about the incident, contact support with details.

Get estimates from qualified repair shops that include:
- Detailed breakdown of damage
- Cost to repair each damaged component  
- Labor costs
- Parts costs

For Deposit Deduction Claims, include estimated damage costs in the claim notes section when ending the rental.

- There is no way to undo the ended rental status

Double-check the booking ID and renter details before ending any rental to avoid this situation.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: What if I forgot to file a deposit deduction claim when ending the rental? ---
If you ended the rental without filing a deposit deduction claim, you cannot go back and add one later. The deposit is automatically refunded to the renter once the rental is ended without a claim. Tell the owner they should have selected the "Deposit Deduction Claim" option when ending the rental. For future reference, always check for damages before ending the rental and file the claim at that time if needed.

Yes, the owner can send repair estimates after filing the initial claim. Tell them: "You can send us the estimate for review when you receive it and we will see what we can do to help you." However, they cannot modify the original deposit deduction claim itself once submitted.

--- [Renter] [damage-claims] Q: I caused damage to a trailer during my rental - what should I do? ---

--- [Both] [damage-claims] Q: Who is responsible for tire damage during a rental? ---
Responsibility depends on the cause:

Renter is responsible for:
• Hitting curbs or road hazards
• Nail or puncture damage  
• Overloading the trailer
• Driving at speeds beyond tire's rated limit
• Any impact-related damage

Owner is responsible for:
• Tires 3+ years old (check DOT date code on sidewall)
• Tire defects
• Low tread depth
• Improper installation
• Normal wear and tear

--- [Renter] [damage-claims] Q: I was in an accident while towing a rental trailer - what do I do? ---

The renter's auto insurance will be responsible for any damage to third-party vehicles. The trailer owner will need to file a claim through Neighbors Trailer for trailer damage.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: A renter damaged my trailer but is disputing the deposit deduction claim - what happens? ---

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: Can I charge a renter for repairs after they've already received their deposit back? ---

However, this requires the renter's card to be valid and not declined. Provide detailed repair receipts and justification for the charges.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: What's the NT Protect insurance deductible? ---

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: A renter is threatening to dispute charges with their credit card company - what should I do? ---

The owner can accept release of funds early by agreeing that if a chargeback is received and lost, the funds will be reversed and taken back from their account. The owner must respond with "I accept" to confirm this agreement.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: My trailer was stolen or abandoned by a renter - what should I do? ---
Report stolen/abandoned trailers immediately to support@neighborstrailer.com. Neighbors Trailer strongly recommends GPS tracking devices on all trailers to help locate them. If the trailer is recovered, document all damages when ending the rental and file appropriate claims. For serious theft cases, Neighbors Trailer may refer the matter to collections.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: The renter returned my trailer but I missed license plate or other damage - can I still claim it? ---

The renter will have 24 hours to respond before the claim is approved.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: A renter broke my trailer door or other expensive component - how do I handle this? ---

If total damages exceed $500 and the booking included insurance, also file an insurance claim through the claims form. Document all damage thoroughly with photos and obtain professional repair estimates to support the full cost of repairs.

--- [Internal] [damage-claims] Q: When should accounts be deactivated for damage claim violations? ---
Deactivate accounts for:
• Multiple fraudulent deposit deduction claims
• Filing claims for pre-existing damage or normal wear/tear  
• Sending out trailers with improper maintenance (e.g., tires over 3 years old)
• Attempting to hide damage attribution between renters
• Pattern of false damage claims

Document specific violations with booking numbers and evidence. Accounts showing 3+ violations across multiple renters warrant immediate deactivation.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: What if I accidentally closed the wrong rental booking? ---
Unfortunately, there is no way to re-open a booking once it has been closed. Tell the owner: "We have no way to re-open a booking once it has been closed." If there are damages to discover when the actual rental ends, they should contact support for assistance with handling the situation.

--- [Renter] [damage-claims] Q: When will I get my security deposit back after returning a trailer? ---
The deposit refund is automatically initiated once the trailer owner ends the booking. It may take 4-7 business days to appear on the renter's statement. If the owner files a deposit deduction claim, the renter has 24 hours to respond before funds are processed.

--- [Both] [damage-claims] Q: Does Neighbors Trailer provide recommendations for repair shops? ---
No, Neighbors Trailer does not have specific repair shop recommendations to provide. Owners must obtain their own repair estimates from local shops. For insurance claims, owners should get estimates promptly but there are no specific deadlines.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: Can I let the renter who damaged my trailer attempt to repair it themselves? ---
This is not recommended. If the renter's repair attempt is not perfect, the owner may reject it and will need to file the insurance claim for professional repairs. It's better to have qualified repair shops handle the work to ensure proper documentation and quality.

--- [Both] [damage-claims] Q: What information is covered in damage claims and when are chargebacks involved? ---
For collections referrals, provide: renter contact information, trailer owner information, details of damage/costs, deposit deduction claim results, and any chargeback disputes. Neighbors Trailer may refer accounts to Debt Collectors International when renters dispute valid damage charges or fail to pay for verified damages.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: How do I report damage when ending a rental? ---
When an owner needs to report damage during the end rental process, direct them to use the Deposit Deduction Claim (DDC) option. Here are the exact steps:

From the app or website when ending the rental:
- Upload a minimum of four new photos of the trailer taken at the time of return
- Confirm the return date and time
- Enter any relevant remarks
- If there is damage, loss, or unpaid rental fees, select the "Deposit Deduction Claim" option (checkbox at the bottom)
- Enter the required damage information and description of how it happened
- Upload images displaying the damages that occurred
- If damages exceed the deposit amount, include the estimated damages in the claim notes
- Then select "End Rental" to complete the process

After DDC submission, the renter gets 24 hours to respond before the claim is automatically approved and money is deposited into the owner's account. If the claim is disputed, staff may ask for additional information or photos.

IMPORTANT: The DDC must be submitted when ending the rental. If an owner already ended the rental without filing a DDC, they can still pursue damage claims by emailing claims@neighborstrailer.com with repair estimates and photos.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: How do I file an insurance claim for trailer damage? ---
Direct owners to file insurance claims only if damages meet or exceed $500 AND the booking included insurance coverage (NT Protect). Before starting the claim, they must gather:

1. Pictures of damages
2. Pictures of all 4 sides of their entire trailer  
3. Picture of the VIN sticker
4. Estimate for repairs

Once they have all documentation, direct them to start their claim at: https://form.jotform.com/Neighbors_Trailer/insurance-claim-form

IMPORTANT: Insurance claims are separate from Deposit Deduction Claims. Owners should first submit a DDC when ending the rental, then file the insurance claim if damages exceed $500. The insurance has a $500 deductible that applies to all eligible claims.

--- [Renter] [damage-claims] Q: How do I dispute a deposit deduction claim? ---
If a renter wants to dispute a deposit deduction claim, tell them they can respond within the 24-hour window after the DDC is submitted. If they need to dispute after that period, they should email service@neighborstrailer.com with their booking ID and explanation.

When processing disputes, staff will review:
- Photos from beginning of rental vs. end of rental
- Owner's damage documentation
- Renter's explanation and any evidence they provide
- Whether damage was pre-existing or occurred during rental

IMPORTANT: Renters should provide specific evidence like videos showing pre-existing damage, timestamps, or detailed explanations of the condition when they picked up the trailer.

--- [Both] [damage-claims] Q: What is the $500 deductible and who pays it? ---
The Protection Package (NT Protect) includes a $500 deductible for all eligible damage claims. Here's how it works:

- Renters pay for the Protection Package at booking (owners are not charged)
- If eligible damages occur, there's a $500 deductible
- The renter is responsible for paying the $500 deductible
- If the deductible cannot be collected from the renter, the trailer owner becomes responsible for the $500 deductible amount

The deductible is typically withheld from the insurance payout, and the renter should pay through their deposit or additional charges.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: Can I report damage after I already ended the rental? ---
Yes. If an owner already ended the rental without filing a Deposit Deduction Claim, they can still pursue damage claims by:

1. Emailing claims@neighborstrailer.com with repair estimates and photos of the damage
2. Staff can process and attempt to charge the renter on the owner's behalf once they provide a repair estimate
3. If damages exceed $500 and the booking had insurance, they can submit an insurance claim once they have the repair estimate
4. They must also provide photos of the damages when submitting the estimate

IMPORTANT: This should be done as soon as possible after discovering the damage. Include the booking ID in all communications.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: What damages can I claim from renters vs. normal wear and tear? ---
Use these guidelines to determine responsibility:

RENTER IS RESPONSIBLE for damage caused during rental:
- Hitting curbs or road hazards
- Nails, punctures, or screws in tires
- Overloading the trailer
- Driving at speeds beyond tire's rated limit
- Any impact-related damage
- Damage to jacks, stands, lights, locks, or other components from misuse
- Side panel damage from impacts

OWNER IS RESPONSIBLE for normal wear and tear:
- Tire damage if tires are 3+ years old (check DOT date code on sidewall)
- Tire defects, low tread, improper installation
- Loose rivets or screws that fall out due to normal use
- General wear from age

For tire age verification: Look for the 4-digit DOT date code on tire sidewall. First two digits = week manufactured, last two digits = year. Example: "2522" = 25th week of 2022.

IMPORTANT: If there's a dispute, staff will review circumstances, photos, and supporting documentation before making a determination.

--- [Both] [damage-claims] Q: How much does NT Protect insurance cover? ---
NT Protect provides coverage up to $25,000 with a $500 deductible for verified rental periods. Coverage details:

Insurance Coverages:
- Comprehensive Coverage: $500 Deductible  
- Collision Coverage: $500 Deductible
- Conversion Coverage: $1,000 Deductible
- Trailer owner liability: $300,000 combined single limit bodily injury and property damage
- Auto Medical Payments: $2,000 per person
- Uninsured Motorists: $15,000 per person / $30,000 each accident bodily injury

IMPORTANT: Insurance policies, coverages and deductibles are set by the insurance company and are subject to change at any time. For full details on coverage including inclusions, exclusions, and other important information, refer renters to the Terms of Use at https://neighborstrailer.com/terms.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: What if my trailer is stolen during a rental? ---
For stolen trailers, direct owners to:

1. File a police report immediately and obtain a copy
2. Contact Neighbors Trailer support with the police report
3. If the renter purchased NT Protect insurance, this may be covered under the policy
4. Staff will provide guidance on filing an insurance claim if applicable

IMPORTANT: Keep copies of all documentation including police reports, booking details, and any communications with the renter. Include the formal police report when available (public versions may be acceptable initially).

--- [Internal] [damage-claims] Q: When should staff charge admin fees on damage claims? ---
Staff should apply a 3.5% admin fee when charging renters for damage claims outside of the normal deposit deduction process. Examples from actual cases:
- $231 tire replacement + $8.08 admin fee
- $90.55 repair + $3.16 admin fee ($93.71 total)

The admin fee appears to apply when staff manually processes damage charges to renter payment methods after the rental has ended.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: How do I get reimbursed for damage that exceeds the deposit? ---
If damage exceeds the deposit amount:

1. Include the estimated damages in the DDC claim notes when ending the rental
2. Email claims@neighborstrailer.com with a detailed repair estimate and photos
3. Staff will attempt to charge the renter for the additional amount beyond the deposit
4. If damage exceeds $500 AND the booking included insurance, file an insurance claim at https://form.jotform.com/Neighbors_Trailer/insurance-claim-form

IMPORTANT: Provide professional repair estimates from certified shops. Include photos showing the specific damage and overall trailer condition. If the renter disputes additional charges, staff will review all evidence before making a determination.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: What should I do about late returns and unpaid rental days? ---
For late returns and unpaid rental days:

1. When ending the rental, select the "Deposit Deduction Claim" option
2. Include both damage claims AND unpaid rental fees in the DDC
3. Document the original return date/time vs. actual return date/time
4. Include late return fees in the claim amount

If the trailer hasn't been returned on time:
1. Message the renter through NT platform asking when they'll return it
2. If no response, text them (request phone number from support if needed)
3. Give a deadline (e.g., "I will give you until ___ time today to contact me or I will escalate")
4. If still no contact, terminate the rental and consider police involvement for recovery

IMPORTANT: Always try to process extension requests before the rental period ends. Late returns without paid extensions can be charged as additional rental days plus any applicable penalties.

--- [Renter] [damage-claims] Q: How do I file a renter claim for damages I incurred during my rental? ---
If a renter needs to file a claim for damages they incurred while using a rental trailer, direct them to contact support at service@neighborstrailer.com. They should include:
- Booking ID number
- Photos of the damage
- Receipts for any repairs they had to make
- Description of what happened

For hub damage, wheel stud failures, or other mechanical issues that occurred during rental, these are typically covered if caused by trailer owner negligence (improper maintenance). Guide the renter to dispute any deposit deduction claim if the owner tries to hold them responsible for pre-existing mechanical issues.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: How do I file a deposit deduction claim when ending a rental? ---
Direct the owner to end the rental properly through their account. When ending the rental:

From Mobile App:
- Select Bookings > Current > [booking] > End Rental
- Upload minimum of 4 new photos taken at time of return
- If there is damage, loss, or unpaid fees, select "Deposit Deduction Claim" option
- Enter required information including damage description and estimated amount
- Then tap End Rental

From Website:
- Dashboard > Bookings > Current Bookings > End Rental
- Upload minimum of 4 new photos taken at time of return  
- If there is damage, check the "Deposit Deduction Claim" box
- Enter required information
- Select End Rental

Important: Once submitted, the renter gets 24 hours to respond before the claim is approved. End the rental immediately when trailer is returned - delays can hurt your case for proving damages.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: I forgot to file a deposit claim when ending the rental - can I still file one? ---
Ask the owner why they ended the rental with remarks stating "Returned without damage" if there actually was damage. If they can provide a valid explanation (oversight, damage discovered later), they may still have options.

For rental completion without damage claims noted, options are limited. If damages exceed $500 and the booking had insurance, they may be able to file an insurance claim. Direct them to use the insurance claim form: https://form.jotform.com/Neighbors_Trailer/insurance-claim-form

Important: Emphasize that ending rentals promptly with accurate damage documentation is critical - waiting makes it difficult to prove damages were caused by the renter.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: How do I file an insurance claim for damages over $500? ---

Required before filing:
1. Pictures of damages
2. Pictures of all 4 sides of entire trailer  
3. Picture of the VIN sticker
4. Estimate for repairs

--- [Both] [damage-claims] Q: How is responsibility for tire damage determined? ---
Also asked as: "Am I responsible for tire damage?", "Who pays for tire replacement?"

Tire damage responsibility depends on the cause:

**Renter is responsible when damage caused by:**
- Hitting curb or road hazard
- Nail or puncture  
- Overloading the trailer
- Driving at speeds beyond tire's rated limit
- Any impact-related damage

**Owner is responsible when damage due to:**
- Tire is 3 years old or older
- Tire defects
- Low tread
- Improper installation

**Checking tire age:** Look for 4-digit DOT code on sidewall. First 2 digits = week manufactured, last 2 digits = year. Example: 2522 = 25th week of 2022.

If there's a dispute about tire age/condition, request photos of the tire showing the DOT code. Staff will review circumstances and supporting documentation to make final determination per Terms of Use.

--- [Renter] [damage-claims] Q: The owner is claiming I'm responsible for tire damage but the tire was old - how do I dispute this? ---
If the renter disputes tire damage responsibility, guide them to provide photos showing the tire's DOT date stamp. If the tire shows manufacture date of 3+ years old, the owner is typically responsible.

Direct them to access their booking and dispute the claim:
1. Dashboard > My Bookings > Past > [booking ID]
2. Scroll to "Booking Activity" > "Deduction Claim"  
3. Select "Contest Claim" and enter comments
4. Upload photos of DOT date stamp if available

Renter has 24 hours from rental completion to dispute. Include any photos taken before/during rental showing tire condition.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: The renter is disputing my tire damage claim - what happens next? ---
When a renter disputes a tire damage claim, review the tire age and damage cause:

If tire shows DOT date of 3+ years old, the claim will likely be dismissed as owner responsibility. If tire is newer, the damage cause determines responsibility:
- Impact damage, punctures, overloading = renter responsibility
- Blowout from age, defects, improper maintenance = owner responsibility

Provide clear photos of the DOT date stamp and damage. Staff will make final determination within 24 hours if no response from disputing party.

--- [Renter] [damage-claims] Q: I had a tire blowout that damaged the trailer fender and side - am I responsible? ---
The responsibility depends on why the tire failed. If the tire blowout was due to:
- Tire age (3+ years old)
- Manufacturing defects  
- Poor maintenance by owner
Then the owner is responsible for all resulting damage.

If blowout was due to renter actions (overloading, excessive speed, impact), then renter may be responsible.

Direct the renter to provide photos of the tire's DOT date stamp and any evidence of the cause. If owner files a deposit claim, the renter should dispute it with this evidence within 24 hours.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: What evidence do I need to support my damage claim? ---
For damage claims to be approved, provide:

**Photos required:**
- Photo from entire side of trailer where damage is located
- Circle the damage areas clearly
- Ensure damage is clearly visible in photos

**DO NOT include:**
- Pictures where trailer is just dirty (can be cleaned)
- Pre-existing damages or normal wear
- Grease stains or normal use marks

**Additional documentation:**
- Before photos from start of rental showing no damage
- Repair estimates if claiming costs
- Timeline of when damage was discovered

Respond within 24 hours when requested or claim may be dismissed. If renter was not present for pickup/return inspection, document this in your notes.

--- [Renter] [damage-claims] Q: How do I dispute a damage claim filed against me? ---
If you receive a deposit deduction claim notification:

1. Access your booking: Dashboard > My Bookings > Past > [booking ID]
2. Find "Booking Activity" section > "Deduction Claim"
3. Select "Contest Claim" 
4. Enter detailed comments explaining why you're not responsible
5. Upload any supporting photos (before photos, evidence of pre-existing damage)

**You have 24 hours** from when the claim was filed to dispute it. Include any evidence such as:
- Photos you took before/during rental
- Evidence of pre-existing damage
- Documentation that damage was due to owner negligence

Staff will review both sides and make a determination.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: How long does the renter have to respond to my damage claim? ---
Renters have 24 hours to respond to or dispute damage claims. After 24 hours with no response, the claim is automatically approved and funds are released to the owner.

If the renter disputes the claim, staff will review both sides and make a determination. This may require additional documentation from both parties.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: The renter returned my trailer late and put excessive miles on it - can I charge for this? ---

- Agreed return time vs actual return time
- Mileage at pickup vs return
- Any prior agreements about mileage limits
- Your established rates for late returns and excess miles

Include these charges in the total amount when filing the deposit deduction claim. If amount exceeds the deposit, you can invoice the renter for additional charges through Neighbors Trailer.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: Can I charge the renter for cleaning if they returned my trailer dirty/with waste? ---
Yes, if the trailer was returned with excessive dirt, debris, or waste (including fecal matter) that requires professional cleaning beyond normal use, include cleaning costs in your deposit deduction claim.

Document with photos showing the uncleaned condition and provide estimate for professional cleaning services. Normal dirt from use is expected, but excessive contamination can be charged to the renter.

--- [Renter] [damage-claims] Q: There was pre-existing damage that wasn't documented - how do I protect myself? ---

2. Message the owner through the platform about the damage
3. Do not proceed if you're uncomfortable with undisclosed damage

For protection during rental:
- Take photos of all sides before pickup
- Document any concerns with owner immediately
- If damage occurs during rental, report it immediately to owner

If owner files claim for pre-existing damage, dispute it within 24 hours using your before photos as evidence.

--- [Owner] [damage-claims] Q: My renter is claiming equipment failure but I think they damaged it - how is this determined? ---
Staff will review the circumstances and evidence from both parties:

**Evidence supporting owner position:**
- Maintenance records showing recent service
- Photos showing impact damage vs. mechanical failure
- Renter admissions of impact/misuse

**Evidence supporting renter position:**
- Age of equipment (bearings, brakes, etc.)
- Maintenance history showing neglect
- Mechanical failure patterns vs. impact damage

For items like hub failures, brake issues, electrical problems - these are often maintenance-related if trailer sees heavy use. Provide maintenance records and service history to support your position.

--- [Internal] [damage-claims] Q: How do I handle a renter who uses abusive language about damage charges? ---
